<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">Madonna singles discography</span></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p>American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> has released 79 <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a> (including 1 as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guest_vocalist" title="Guest vocalist">featured artist</a>) and 15 <a href="/wiki/Promotional_recording" title="Promotional recording">promotional singles</a>. In 1982, Madonna signed a contract with <a href="/wiki/Sire_Records" title="Sire Records">Sire Records</a>, and released her first two singles before launching her eponymous <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(Madonna_album)" title="Madonna (Madonna album)">debut album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Her first entry on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> was "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_(Madonna_song)" title="Holiday (Madonna song)">Holiday</a>" (1983), which peaked at number 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-holiday_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-holiday-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, Madonna released "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>", which reached number one in Australia, Canada and the US; the latter it spent six weeks atop the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The album <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin" title="Like a Virgin">Like a Virgin</a></i> spawned three other top five singles: "<a href="/wiki/Material_Girl" title="Material Girl">Material Girl</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Angel_(Madonna_song)" title="Angel (Madonna song)">Angel</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Dress_You_Up" title="Dress You Up">Dress You Up</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1985 Madonna released her second US number-one single, "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_for_You_(Madonna_song)" title="Crazy for You (Madonna song)">Crazy for You</a>", and her first UK number-one single, "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Groove" title="Into the Groove">Into the Groove</a>", both from motion picture soundtracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Following year, Madonna's third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_album)" title="True Blue (Madonna album)">True Blue</a></i>, gave her three number-one singles: "<a href="/wiki/Live_to_Tell" title="Live to Tell">Live to Tell</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Papa_Don%27t_Preach" title="Papa Don't Preach">Papa Don't Preach</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Open_Your_Heart_(Madonna_song)" title="Open Your Heart (Madonna song)">Open Your Heart</a>". Two other singles from the album, "<a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_song)" title="True Blue (Madonna song)">True Blue</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/La_Isla_Bonita" title="La Isla Bonita">La Isla Bonita</a>", were top-five hits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1987, she scored another number-one single with "<a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_(Madonna_song)" title="Who's That Girl (Madonna song)">Who's That Girl</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(song)" title="Like a Prayer (song)">title track</a> from Madonna's fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(album)" title="Like a Prayer (album)">Like a Prayer</a></i> (1989), reached number one, making her the first artist to accumulate seven number-one singles in the 1980s, and the first female performer to get as many number-ones as a solo act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Other top ten singles from <i>Like a Prayer</i> included "<a href="/wiki/Express_Yourself_(Madonna_song)" title="Express Yourself (Madonna song)">Express Yourself</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Cherish_(Madonna_song)" title="Cherish (Madonna song)">Cherish</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Keep_It_Together_(Madonna_song)" title="Keep It Together (Madonna song)">Keep It Together</a>". By the end of the decade, she was tied with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> as the artist with the most number one songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1990, Madonna released "<a href="/wiki/Vogue_(Madonna_song)" title="Vogue (Madonna song)">Vogue</a>" from the album <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_Breathless" title="I'm Breathless">I'm Breathless</a></i>, which topped the charts in all major music markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> "Vogue" was followed by "<a href="/wiki/Justify_My_Love" title="Justify My Love">Justify My Love</a>" and soundtrack single, "<a href="/wiki/This_Used_to_Be_My_Playground" title="This Used to Be My Playground">This Used to Be My Playground</a>", becoming her subsequent chart topping songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Her fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Erotica_(Madonna_album)" title="Erotica (Madonna album)">Erotica</a></i>, was released in 1992, but failed to generate any chart-topping singles. Only the <a href="/wiki/Erotica_(song)" title="Erotica (song)">title track</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Deeper_and_Deeper" title="Deeper and Deeper">Deeper and Deeper</a>" reached the top ten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1995, Madonna released "<a href="/wiki/Take_a_Bow_(Madonna_song)" title="Take a Bow (Madonna song)">Take a Bow</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Bedtime_Stories_(Madonna_album)" title="Bedtime Stories (Madonna album)">Bedtime Stories</a></i>, her sixth studio album. The song became her biggest hit on the Hot 100 and stayed on the top for seven weeks, making it her longest run at number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Frozen_(Madonna_song)" title="Frozen (Madonna song)">Frozen</a>", from the 1998 studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i> became her first ever single to debut at number-one in the United Kingdom. It was also her first chart topper there since 1990, and marked a major comeback for her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light_(song)" title="Ray of Light (song)">title track</a> reached the top-ten in the United States, the United Kingdom, Australia, Canada, and Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, Madonna scored her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_artists_by_number_of_Billboard_Hot_100_number_one_singles" title="List of artists by number of Billboard Hot 100 number one singles">12th US number-one single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>", from the album of the <a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_album)" title="Music (Madonna album)">same name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna released her ninth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/American_Life" title="American Life">American Life</a></i> (2003), whose singles failed to achieve commercial success. "<a href="/wiki/Hung_Up" title="Hung Up">Hung Up</a>", from her tenth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor" title="Confessions on a Dance Floor">Confessions on a Dance Floor</a></i> (2005), became her biggest worldwide hit song. It peaked at number one in 41 countries and earned a place in the 2007 <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> for topping the charts in more countries than any other song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guiness_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-guiness-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> With "Hung Up" going <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a>, Madonna surpassed <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> for having most gold certified singles in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Sorry_(Madonna_song)" title="Sorry (Madonna song)">Sorry</a>", became Madonna's 12th number-one single on the UK charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/4_Minutes_(Madonna_song)" title="4 Minutes (Madonna song)">4 Minutes</a>", the lead single from her 11th studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hard_Candy_(Madonna_album)" title="Hard Candy (Madonna album)">Hard Candy</a></i>, scored Madonna her 37th <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 top-ten hit, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> as the artist with the most top-ten singles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> She extended the record with the number ten reaching "<a href="/wiki/Give_Me_All_Your_Luvin%27" title="Give Me All Your Luvin'">Give Me All Your Luvin'</a>", from her 2012 studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/MDNA_(album)" title="MDNA (album)">MDNA</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna ended the 2000s as the best-selling physical singles artist of the decade in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> She was announced as the highest ranking solo artist on the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_All-Time_Top_Artists" title="Billboard Hot 100 All-Time Top Artists"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 All-Time Top Artists</a>" as well as having most number-one singles in the United Kingdom amongst female artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna has a record 156 number-one singles across all formats of the <i>Billboard</i> charts, the most for any artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> She is also the most successful artist on <i>Billboard</i> '​s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Play" title="Hot Dance Club Play">Hot Dance Club Play</a> chart with a total of 43 number-one singles, and is the only active artist to chart continuously since 1982, spanning four decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> As of February 2008, she has sold more than 115 million singles globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<tr>
<td colspan="15" style="font-size:90%">"—" denotes a title that did not chart, or was not released in that territory.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><b>A</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_a1"><b><a href="#ref_note_a1">^</a></b></span> "Everybody" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 but peaked on the <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100_Singles" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles">Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles</a> chart at number seven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>B</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_b1"><b><a href="#ref_note_b1">^</a></b></span> "Burning Up" charted on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Play</a> chart as a <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side#Double_A-side" title="A-side and B-side">double A-side</a> single with "Physical Attraction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>C</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_c1"><b><a href="#ref_note_c1">^</a></b></span> "Holiday" has been released in the United Kingdom on three separate occasions – January 14, 1984 release reached position six, then re-issued on July 30, 1985 when it reached number two and the final re-release was on June 4, 1991 with an additional <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> version <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Holiday_Collection_(EP)" title="The Holiday Collection (EP)">The Holiday Collection</a></i>. It reached five on the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-uk-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>D</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_d1"><b><a href="#ref_note_d1">^</a></b></span> "Lucky Star" was originally released in the United Kingdom in September 1983, bubbling under the UK Singles Chart at number 171. It was re-issued there in March 1984 and peaked at number 14. It charted on the Hot Dance Club Play chart as a double A-side single with "Holiday".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>E</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_e1"><b><a href="#ref_note_e1">^</a></b></span> "Borderline" originally reached fifty-six in the UK, but reached a new peak of two when re-released in January 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_38-5"><a href="#cite_note-uk-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>F</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_f1"><b><a href="#ref_note_f1">^</a></b></span> "Crazy for You" was re-released in the UK as "Crazy For You (Remix)" on February 24, 1991. It was the second single there from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Collection" title="The Immaculate Collection">The Immaculate Collection</a></i>. Both the releases reached number two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_38-6"><a href="#cite_note-uk-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>G</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_g1"><b><a href="#ref_note_g1">^</a></b></span> "Into the Groove" was not commercially released in North America and is not included on the US version of <i>Like a Virgin</i>. It is only available as the B-side of "Angel", therefore it was ineligible to enter the Hot 100 or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Singles_Sales" title="Hot Singles Sales">Hot 100 Singles Sales</a> charts. It charted as a double A-side single with "Angel" in Australia and the Hot Dance Club Play chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>H</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_h1"><b><a href="#ref_note_h1">^</a></b></span> A <a href="/wiki/Gramophone_record" title="Gramophone record">vinyl</a> maxi DJ-set of the remix compilation <i>You Can Dance</i> charted on <i>Billboard</i> '​s Hot Dance Club Play chart as "You Can Dance (LP Cuts)", eventually reaching the top of the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_29-13"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>I</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_i1"><b><a href="#ref_note_i1">^</a></b></span> "Oh Father" was released in the UK on December 27, 1995, as the second single from <i>Something to Remember</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_38-7"><a href="#cite_note-uk-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>J</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_j1"><b><a href="#ref_note_j1">^</a></b></span> "Keep It Together" was released as a double A-side in Australia with "Vogue". The latter song was initially supposed to be a B-side for the former, but Warner Bros. decided to change it as a single after noting its potential as a hit record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>K</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_k1"><b><a href="#ref_note_k1">^</a></b></span> "Love Don't Live Here Anymore" was originally released on March 10, 1986 in Japan only. The version released in 1995 was remixed by David Reitzas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>L</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_l1"><b><a href="#ref_note_l1">^</a></b></span> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_l2"><b><a href="#ref_note_l2">^</a></b></span> "Beautiful Stranger" and "American Pie" were not commercially released in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>M</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_m1"><b><a href="#ref_note_m1">^</a></b></span> "Hollywood" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 or the Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-al-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>N</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_n1"><b><a href="#ref_note_n1">^</a></b></span> "Nothing Fails" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 or the Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-al-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> It was considered an EP in Australia and was only eligible for the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Albums Chart</a>. It charted at six on the ARIA Dance Albums chart in December 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ariadance_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-ariadance-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>O</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_o1"><b><a href="#ref_note_o1">^</a></b></span> "Love Profusion" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 or the Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al_124-2"><a href="#cite_note-al-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> It was originally released in Australia, Italy and the United Kingdom on November 21, 2003. It was later released in North America and France on March 16, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ariadance_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-ariadance-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>P</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_p1"><b><a href="#ref_note_p1">^</a></b></span> "Get Together" and "Jump" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 but entered the Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles Chart at positions six and five respectively. "Get Together" also peaked at number eighty-four on the now discontinued <a href="/wiki/Pop_100" title="Pop 100">Pop 100</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Q</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_q1"><b><a href="#ref_note_q1">^</a></b></span> "Girl Gone Wild" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 but entered the Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles Chart at number six.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotional_singles">Promotional singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_singles_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Promotional singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col" width="200px">Song</th>
<th scope="col">Year</th>
<th scope="col">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Now I'm Following You"</th>
<td>1990</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Originally to be released as the third and final single from <i>I'm Breathless</i>, with remixes commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Saunders" title="Mark Saunders">Mark Saunders</a>, it was cancelled due to the release of <i>The Immaculate Collection</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Erotic"</th>
<td>1992</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Promotional CD available with the 1992 publication, <i><a href="/wiki/Sex_(book)" title="Sex (book)">Sex</a></i>. This version was created at the end of the <i>Erotica</i> sessions and includes additional lyrics not available on the album version. These lyrics were also used in the <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a> remixes on the "Erotica" single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show</a>"</th>
<td>1994</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Promotional CD available with the 1994 <i>The Girlie Show</i> publication, charting <a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show World Tour</a> in 1993. It included three live tracks: "Like a Virgin", "In This Life" and "Why's It So Hard" which were recorded during <i><a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show:_Live_Down_Under" title="The Girlie Show: Live Down Under">The Girlie Show: Live Down Under</a></i> in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/I_Want_You_(Marvin_Gaye_song)" title="I Want You (Marvin Gaye song)">I Want You</a>" <small>(with <a href="/wiki/Massive_Attack" title="Massive Attack">Massive Attack</a>)</small></th>
<td>1995</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Originally to be the first single from the compilation <i>Something to Remember</i>, cancelled due to contract problems with <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown Records</a>, the copyright owners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Buenos Aires" <small>(remixes)</small></th>
<td>1997</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Originally to be the fourth and final single from <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(soundtrack)" title="Evita (soundtrack)">Evita</a></i>, remixes were commissioned from <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Flores" title="Pablo Flores">Pablo Flores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javier_Garza" title="Javier Garza">Javier Garza</a> but the release was cancelled and only available as a promotional 12" vinyl. The remixes charted on the Hot Dance Club Play at number three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotdance_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-hotdance-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Sky Fits Heaven" <small>(remixes)</small></th>
<td>1998</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>From the 1998 studio album <i>Ray of Light</i>. Remixes by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Calderone" title="Victor Calderone">Victor Calderone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sasha_(DJ)" title="Sasha (DJ)">Sasha</a> appear as B-side to the 1998 single "Drowned World/Substitute for Love". Commercial release led to the remixes charting on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Dance Club Play chart at forty-one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotdance_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-hotdance-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Impressive_Instant" title="Impressive Instant">Impressive Instant</a>" <small>(remixes)</small></th>
<td rowspan="2">2001</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>From the 2000 studio album <i>Music</i>. Remix by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Rauhofer" title="Peter Rauhofer">Peter Rauhofer</a> from his live compilation album <i>Live @ Roxy Vol. 4</i>, reached the peak of number one on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Dance Club Play due to heavy club play. Promo one-track in-house CD was sent to clubs including the Peter Rauhofer Universal Club Mix.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotdance_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-hotdance-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GHV2_Megamix" title="GHV2 Megamix">GHV2 Megamix</a>"</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>A remix featuring snippets of the songs on the 2001 compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/GHV2" title="GHV2">GHV2</a></i>. Remixes by <a href="/wiki/Thunderpuss" title="Thunderpuss">Thunderpuss</a> charted on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Dance Club Play at five. Other remixes were created by Tracy Young, Johnny Rocks and Mac Quayle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotdance_132-3"><a href="#cite_note-hotdance-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Hollywood_(Madonna_song)#Remixes" title="Hollywood (Madonna song)">Into the Hollywood Groove</a>"</th>
<td rowspan="2">2003</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>A remix of "Into the Groove" and "Hollywood" featuring <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>. It was created as part of a commercial campaign for clothing retailer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gap_(clothing_retailer)" title="Gap (clothing retailer)">GAP</a> and copies of the promotional CD were given away to customers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Nobody_Knows_Me" title="Nobody Knows Me">Nobody Knows Me</a>" <small>(remixes)</small></th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>From the 2003 studio album <i>American Life</i>. A promotional 12" vinyl with remixes by Peter Rauhofer, <a href="/wiki/Above_%26_Beyond_(band)" title="Above &amp; Beyond (band)">Above &amp; Beyond</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Sims" title="Mount Sims">Mount Sims</a> was sent to clubs and charted at four on the Hot Dance Club Play. Later some of the mixes were released on the "Love Profusion" single in Europe and also on the remix compilation <i>Remixed &amp; Revisited</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotdance_132-4"><a href="#cite_note-hotdance-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Imagine" <small>(Live)</small></th>
<td rowspan="2">2005</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Madonna performed the cover of the <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> song at the <a href="/wiki/Tsunami_Aid" title="Tsunami Aid">Tsunami Aid: Concert of Hope</a> in January 2005. Her performance was available as a digital download on the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Connect" title="Sony Connect">Sony Connect</a> website the following day of the concert. All proceeds from the downloads went to the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> charity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> This version was later included on the live album <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_Going_to_Tell_You_a_Secret#CD_track_listing" title="I'm Going to Tell You a Secret">I'm Going to Tell You a Secret</a></i> and another live recording on the 2005 promotional <i>Q Magazine Presents John Lennon Covered</i> given away as a free gift CD with <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q</a></i> magazine to celebrate Lennon's 65th birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Mother and Father" <small>(remixes)</small></th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>From the 2003 studio album <i>American Life</i> and Peter Rauhofer's compilation <i>Live @ Roxy Vol. 4</i>. His remix charted at nine on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Dance Club Play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotdance_132-5"><a href="#cite_note-hotdance-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Hey_You_(Madonna_song)" title="Hey You (Madonna song)">Hey You</a>"</th>
<td>2007</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>A charity song released as part of the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth" title="Live Earth">Live Earth</a> campaign. It was initially released as a free download for a period of seven days before being made available as a regular digital single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Hey You" entered the charts in some countries, reaching number 57 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> number 55 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Music_Charts" title="Swiss Music Charts">Swiss Singles Chart</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> and number 187 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Broken"</th>
<td rowspan="2">2012</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Written by Madonna, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Oakenfold" title="Paul Oakenfold">Paul Oakenfold</a>, Ian Green and Ciaran Gribbin and produced by Madonna and Oakenfold. The song was recorded during the <i>Celebration</i> sessions. Icon official fanclub members were given a special 12" vinyl single of the track with unique artwork as a part of their membership. It was announced in August 2011, but was actually supposed to be given as a gift in 2010. The single was eventually given to members in late 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Superstar_(Madonna_song)" title="Superstar (Madonna song)">Superstar</a>"</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Released on December 3, 2012 in Brazil as a special edition free CD with Brazilian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S._Paulo" title="Folha de S. Paulo">Folha de S. Paulo</a></i>. The accompanying artwork for the single was created by Brazilian graffitist Simone Sapienza who won a contest sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Johnnie_Walker" title="Johnnie Walker">Johnnie Walker</a>'s Keep Walking Project in Brazil, she was chosen by Madonna after being among ten finalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_appearances">Other appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_singles_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col" width="200px">Song</th>
<th scope="col">Year</th>
<th scope="col">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Ain't No Big Deal"</th>
<td rowspan="2">1984</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Written by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Bray" title="Stephen Bray">Stephen Bray</a> and produced by <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Lucas" title="Reggie Lucas">Reggie Lucas</a>, it was recorded during the <i>Madonna</i> studio album sessions and appeared on the 1984 Warner Bros. compilation <i>Revenge of the Killer B's Vol. 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Originally it was to be included on the studio album and planned as the b-side to "Everybody", this never materialized, instead it was later included as a AA maxi-single in Japan with "Dress You Up" in 1985<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> and also as the b-side to the "True Blue" in some countries in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Sidewalk_Talk" title="Sidewalk Talk">Sidewalk Talk</a>"</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Recorded and released by record producer <a href="/wiki/John_Benitez" title="John Benitez">John "Jellybean" Benitez</a>, as a single from his album <i>Wotupski!?!</i>. Madonna wrote the song and is featured on the chorus. It also appeared on the compilation titled <i>80's Dance Hits</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Each_Time_You_Break_My_Heart" title="Each Time You Break My Heart">Each Time You Break My Heart</a>"</th>
<td>1986</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Performed by <a href="/wiki/Nick_Kamen" title="Nick Kamen">Nick Kamen</a> from his self-titled debut album. Madonna wrote and produced the song with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Bray" title="Stephen Bray">Stephen Bray</a>, and sings the backing vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Santa_Baby" title="Santa Baby">Santa Baby</a>"</th>
<td>1987</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Appears on the album <i><a href="/wiki/A_Very_Special_Christmas_(album)" title="A Very Special Christmas (album)">A Very Special Christmas</a></i> and was produced by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> It remains Madonna's best-selling non-single track to date, selling 189,000 digital downloads according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/I_Surrender_Dear" title="I Surrender Dear">I Surrender Dear</a>"</th>
<td>1989</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>A duet with <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Grey" title="Jennifer Grey">Jennifer Grey</a>, appears in the 1989 film <i><a href="/wiki/Bloodhounds_of_Broadway_(1989_film)" title="Bloodhounds of Broadway (1989 film)">Bloodhounds of Broadway</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Get Over"</th>
<td rowspan="2">1992</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Performed by <a href="/wiki/Nick_Scotti" title="Nick Scotti">Nick Scotti</a>, where Madonna sang prominent, almost duet-style vocals. The song was written and produced by Madonna and <a href="/wiki/Shep_Pettibone" title="Shep Pettibone">Shep Pettibone</a> and released as the second single from Nick Scotti's self-titled album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Supernatural" <small>(Original Arms House Mix)</small></th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Remix of the song originally recorded during the <i>Like a Prayer</i> album sessions. The remix was created by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sly_%26_Robbie" title="Sly &amp; Robbie">Sly &amp; Robbie</a> and was created for the benefit compilation <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_%2B_Dance" title="Red Hot + Dance">Red Hot + Dance</a></i>. The original version of the song had previously appeared as the b-side to the 1989 single "<a href="/wiki/Cherish_(Madonna_song)" title="Cherish (Madonna song)">Cherish</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Goodbye to Innocence"</th>
<td>1994</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Appears on the Sire Records compilation <i>Just Say Roe: Volume VII of Just Say Yes</i>, recorded in 1992 during the <i>Erotica</i> album sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Earlier in 1993, a dub extended remix of the song titled "Up Down Suite" appeared on the single release of "<a href="/wiki/Rain_(Madonna_song)" title="Rain (Madonna song)">Rain</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Freedom"</th>
<td rowspan="2">1995</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Appears on the compilation <i>Carnival!: Rainforest Foundation Concert</i>, recorded in 1994 during the <i>Bedtime Stories</i> album sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Guilty By Association"</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>A duet by Madonna and her brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Joe_Henry" title="Joe Henry">Joe Henry</a> on the charity album <i><a href="/wiki/Sweet_Relief_II:_Gravity_of_the_Situation" title="Sweet Relief II: Gravity of the Situation">Sweet Relief II: Gravity of the Situation</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Love_Won%27t_Wait" title="Love Won't Wait">Love Won't Wait</a>"</th>
<td>1997</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Written by Madonna and <a href="/wiki/Shep_Pettibone" title="Shep Pettibone">Shep Pettibone</a>, the song was recorded by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Barlow" title="Gary Barlow">Gary Barlow</a> and released as the second single from his debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Open_Road_(Gary_Barlow_album)" title="Open Road (Gary Barlow album)">Open Road</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Bittersweet"</th>
<td>1998</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Appears on <a href="/wiki/Deepak_Chopra" title="Deepak Chopra">Deepak Chopra</a>'s album <i>Gift of Love: Music Inspired by Rumi Love Poem</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Be Careful (Cuidado Con Mi Corazon)"</th>
<td>1999</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>A duet with <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a> which appears on his album <i><a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin_(1999_album)" title="Ricky Martin (1999 album)">Ricky Martin</a></i>, it was written and produced by Madonna and <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Time Stood Still"</th>
<td>2000</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Appears on the <a href="/wiki/The_Next_Best_Thing" title="The Next Best Thing">soundtrack</a> for the 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Best_Thing" title="The Next Best Thing">The Next Best Thing</a></i>, it was written and produced by Madonna and William Orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Skin" <small>(The Collaboration Mix)</small></th>
<td>2001</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Remix of the song from <i>Ray of Light</i> (1998). The remix was created by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Calderone" title="Victor Calderone">Victor Calderone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Rauhofer" title="Peter Rauhofer">Peter Rauhofer</a> and appears exclusively on the former's remix compilation <i>E=VC2 Volume 2</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Mi Abbandono A Te"</th>
<td>2004</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Written by Madonna and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Nowels" title="Rick Nowels">Rick Nowels</a>, the song was recorded by Italian singer <a href="/wiki/Laura_Pausini" title="Laura Pausini">Laura Pausini</a> for her 2004 album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resta_In_Ascolto" title="Resta In Ascolto">Resta In Ascolto</a></i>. The song is based on an unreleased demo "Like a Flower" recorded during the <i>Ray of Light</i> sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"<a href="/wiki/Sing_(Annie_Lennox_song)" title="Sing (Annie Lennox song)">Sing</a>"</th>
<td rowspan="2">2007</td>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Performed by <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a> on her album, <i><a href="/wiki/Songs_of_Mass_Destruction" title="Songs of Mass Destruction">Songs of Mass Destruction</a></i>. Madonna sang one verse and back-up vocals with 22 other artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">"Alone Again"</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Written by Madonna along with <a href="/wiki/Rick_Nowels" title="Rick Nowels">Rick Nowels</a>, the song was recorded by Australian singer <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a> for her 2007 documentary film, <i><a href="/wiki/White_Diamond:_A_Personal_Portrait_of_Kylie_Minogue" title="White Diamond: A Personal Portrait of Kylie Minogue">White Diamond: A Personal Portrait of Kylie Minogue</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
